## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (batch reactor / concentration-time dynamics)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is the time-derivative of a chemical species concentration A(t), which is the standard object modeled by reaction rate laws in chemical kinetics. With only t and A available, the most likely structures are single-species consumption/production ODEs with concentration-dependent reaction order and possibly time-varying effective rate constants (e.g., due to temperature programs or catalyst deactivation).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order rate law (constant-rate consumption/production): dA_dt = c0 (e.g., saturation-limited regime where rate is independent of A over a range)
- First-order decay/consumption: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay, pseudo-first-order conditions)
- n-th order (power-law) kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (empirical reaction order / mass-action-like with unknown order)
- Second-order decay (bimolecular/self-reaction): dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (e.g., 2A -> products, or pseudo-second-order fit)
- Mixed/parallel pathways (linear + quadratic): dA_dt = -c0 * A - c1 * A**2 (simultaneous first- and second-order channels)
- Autocatalytic-type polynomial rate: dA_dt = c0 * A - c1 * A**2 (net growth at low A with self-limitation; can represent autocatalysis with depletion/termination lumped)
- Relaxation to equilibrium concentration: dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) (approach to steady state A = c1, e.g., reversible reaction lumped into first-order relaxation)
- Bistable / multiple fixed points (cubic kinetics): dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) * (A - c2) * (A - c3) (phenomenological kinetics with multiple steady states)
- Time-varying first-order rate (linear ramp in effective k): dA_dt = -(c0 + c1 * t) * A (temperature ramp, changing catalyst activity, or evolving medium effects approximated linearly)
- Time-varying first-order rate (exponential change in effective k): dA_dt = -c0 * exp(c1 * t) * A (strongly time-dependent conditions such as programmed heating or deactivation/activation trends)
- Catalyst deactivation / aging (hyperbolically decreasing k): dA_dt = -(c0 / (1 + c1 * t)) * A (effective rate constant decreases with time-on-stream)
- Driven system with source + sink: dA_dt = c0 - c1 * A (continuous generation of A with first-order removal; common lumped model for feed/leak/formation plus consumption)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Consumption of a reactant A typically implies dA_dt < 0 over most of the trajectory; sign consistency is a strong diagnostic for decay-type laws.
- If the magnitude |dA_dt| scales approximately proportionally with A, first-order structure (-c0*A) is likely; curvature in semi-log A vs t supports this.
- If decay is very fast at high A but slows dramatically as A decreases, higher-order terms (e.g., -c0*A**2 or -c0*A**c1 with c1>1) are plausible.
- A nonzero steady state A ≈ constant suggests a relaxation form -c0*(A-c1) or a source–sink balance c0 - c1*A rather than pure decay.
- If early-time behavior differs systematically from late-time behavior at the same A level, the effective rate constant likely depends on t (k(t) * A forms).
- Evidence of two distinct kinetic regimes (e.g., initially linear in A then strongly nonlinear) can indicate mixed pathways -c0*A - c1*A**2.
- Multiple crossings where dA_dt changes sign at different A values indicate multiple fixed points, motivating factored polynomials like (A-c1)(A-c2)...
- If A initially increases before decreasing (or vice versa) without external variables, autocatalytic-like polynomial structures (c0*A - c1*A**2) can capture the turnover behavior.

GT Equivalence Verification (CRK12)

GT: -c0*A*exp(-c1*_s*t) + c2*_t*sin(log(A + c3))
Candidates evaluated: 50
Matched candidate IDs: []
Matched candidates: []

I need to determine which candidates can exactly match the Ground Truth:

**GT:** `-0.4537*A*exp(-0.08462*t) + 0.7535*sin(log(A + 1))`

The GT has two terms:
1. `A*exp(c*t)` — an exponential decay in t multiplied by A
2. `sin(log(A + 1))` — a sine of logarithm function of A

The key challenge is the `sin(log(A+1))` term. This is a very specific transcendental function. Let me check which candidates contain basis functions that could represent this.

**Critical observation:** `sin(log(A+1))` cannot be represented by:
- Polynomials in A
- `exp(A*c)` terms
- `log(A*c + 1)` terms (these are logarithms, not sine of logarithms)
- `1/(A+c)` rational terms
- `A^c` power terms
- `1/sqrt(A+c)` terms
- `A*c/(A*c+c)` rational terms

The function `sin(log(A+1))` is an oscillatory function that none of the standard basis functions (polynomials, exponentials, logarithms, rational functions, power functions) can exactly reproduce. It requires either an explicit `sin(log(...))` term or a `sin(...)` combined with `log(...)` in the right way.

Let me scan all candidates for any that contain `sin`:

- **Candidate 12:** Contains `c2*sin(A*c3 + c4)` — this is `sin(linear function of A)`, NOT `sin(log(A+1))`. These are fundamentally different functions and cannot be made equivalent.

- **Candidate 44:** Contains `log(A*c7 + 1)` terms multiplied by polynomials in A, divided by `(A+c1)`. No sine function present.

None of the candidates contain `sin(log(...))`. The only candidate with `sin` is Candidate 12, which has `sin(A*c3 + c4)` — a sine of a linear function, not a sine of a logarithm.

Since `sin(log(A+1))` is linearly independent from all the basis functions present in any candidate (polynomials, exponentials, logarithms, rational functions, power functions, sqrt), and `sin(c*A + c)` ≠ `sin(log(A+1))` for all A, **no candidate can match the GT**.

Let me verify Candidate 12 more carefully: `A*c0*exp(c1*t) + A + c2*sin(A*c3 + c4) + c5/(A + c6) + c7/(A*c8 + c6)`. The `sin(A*c3 + c4)` term oscillates with period `2π/c3` in A, while `sin(log(A+1))` has decreasing frequency as A increases. These are fundamentally different functions.
